[14.02.26, 03:30:47] Paisanurture.in, CFP (Certified Financial Planner): 🔍 How to Read a Physical Water Meter at Home

Most water meters are mechanical with black and red digits.

1️⃣ Look at the black numbers

These represent kilolitres (KL) or cubic meters (m³)

1 cubic meter (1 m³) = 1000 litres

2️⃣ Ignore red digits (usually decimals)

Red digits show litres (smaller units)

For billing, usually only black digits are considered

Example:

If your meter shows:

004000.23

004000 → Billable reading

.23 → Decimal (generally ignored for billing)

💧 In Your Case

Your meter moved from 3000 to 4000, meaning:

1000 litres used

That equals 1 kilolitre (KL)
[14.02.26, 03:31:00] Paisanurture.in, CFP (Certified Financial Planner): 📌 Water Meter Readings on Your Bill

Previous Reading: 3000

Present Reading: 4000

Consumption: 1000 litres (or units as per meter type)

✅ How It Is Calculated

Water consumption =
Present Reading – Previous Reading

4000
−
3000
=
1000
4000−3000=1000

So, you have used 1000 units (litres) of water during this billing period.
